  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a338dd12-9127-4e30-861d-5edeaa7260e4'

<span id="freeTextContainer8804292980262479310"><b>A heartwarming and refreshing debut novel that proves one thing: there's not enough data in the world to predict what will make your heart tick.</b><br/><br/>Stella Lane thinks math is the only thing that unites the universe.   <span id="freeText8804292980262479310" style="display:none"><b>A heartwarming and refreshing debut novel that proves one thing: there's not enough data in the world to predict what will make your heart tick.</b><br /><br />Stella Lane thinks math is the only thing that unites the universe. She comes up with algorithms to predict customer purchases — a job that has given her more money than she knows what to do with, and way less experience in the dating department than the average thirty-year-old.<br /><br />It doesn't help that Stella has Asperger's and French kissing reminds her of a shark getting its teeth cleaned by pilot fish. Her conclusion: she needs lots of practice — with a professional. Which is why she hires escort Michael Phan. The Vietnamese and Swedish stunner can't afford to turn down Stella's offer, and agrees to help her check off all the boxes on her lesson plan — from foreplay to more-than-missionary position...<br /><br />Before long, Stella not only learns to appreciate his kisses, but to crave all the other things he's making her feel. Soon, their no-nonsense partnership starts making a strange kind of sense. And the pattern that emerges will convince Stella that love is the best kind of logic...</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I know the the author expressed her feelings on this but I couldn’t help thinking of Stella as Asian or half Asian half white. I think it was her pare<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I know the the author expressed her feelings on this but I couldn’t help thinking of Stella as Asian or half Asian half white. I think it was her parents who had such high expectations of her (totally stereotyping in my head) and also the fact that she was aware of wuxia and Asian actors. Or maybe I’m getting their POV’s mixed up in my head.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/3102847-jill"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_100x100-6433b08cbe793211f55e184d39e84c4d.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/3102847-jill">Jill</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It is graphic, which I normally don't like. In this case, sex is the raison d'etre for our two people to meet. The sex scenes are really well written,<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It is graphic, which I normally don't like. In this case, sex is the raison d'etre for our two people to meet. The sex scenes are really well written, better written, in my opinion, than just about any others I've read. Normally, I skip over the graphic parts, but in this book, I devoured every word. Can't wait for her next book.<br /><a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_2543996363" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2543996363" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2543996363?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=poc-rep">poc-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=own-voices">own-voices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult-contemporary">adult-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=2018-releases">2018-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult-romance">adult-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2543996363" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4140342267078987955">This book had the nerve…the audacity…the unmitigated gall…to come into <em>my</em> home…where <em>I</em> pay the bills…and <em>let me down</em>.<br/><br/>On the bright side, however, at least it’s not a Percy Jackson movie.<br/><br/>I relish stories that give voices to cultures and experiences that are unfortunately too rarely represented on page or screen, so when I heard this book is an ownvoices story about a woman with Asperger's, I immediately added it to my TBR.<br/><br/>Although this novel isn't as winning as I expected it to be, there's certai</span>
  <span id="freeText4140342267078987955" style="display:none">This book had the nerve…the audacity…the unmitigated gall…to come into <em>my</em> home…where <em>I</em> pay the bills…and <em>let me down</em>.<br /><br />On the bright side, however, at least it’s not a Percy Jackson movie.<br /><br />I relish stories that give voices to cultures and experiences that are unfortunately too rarely represented on page or screen, so when I heard this book is an ownvoices story about a woman with Asperger's, I immediately added it to my TBR.<br /><br />Although this novel isn't as winning as I expected it to be, there's certainly plenty to admire in it: the fact that this is a book version of <em>Pretty Women </em>but with a refreshing subversion that’s embodied in the gender role reversal, the exploration of money and how fortune doesn’t touch everyone with the same hand which was by turns careful and unflinching, how there’s a real sense of culture and history in the depiction of Michael’s community (his Vietnamese heritage shines through and there's tremendous joy in his interaction with his family: the banter, the support, the kindness threaded through pitiless teasing), and the knowledge that the events in this book and the author’s continued research has inspired her to seek out a therapist and be diagnosed on the spectrum. It's very important to see autistic women at the forefront of efforts at representation, expanding the conversation and the vision for autistic characters.<br /><br />That said, I fault this book for many things—each one jabbing at my initial excitement, until it deflated completely. I fault it for being boring, averagely written and riddled with clichés. Most important, though, I fault it for demonstrating knowledge of important issues only to lampshade the significance of its premise rather than delve deeper into something more nuanced. I expected more from this—more rigor, more thoughtfulness, more craft. Instead, I was left staggered and uncertain how to feel about the whole thing—about an ending that felt trivial, almost mocking the seriousness of the rest of the book, and a fizz of uneasiness that I couldn’t quite shake afterwards.<br /><br />This is the story of a woman who was smart and beautiful and accomplished, and who simply had the poor fortune of coming across men who had never cared for more than their own entertainment, who didn’t have her welfare anywhere remotely near at heart and who treated her more like a boring convenience than an exciting toy. So, she stood there and accepted the weight of the blame, because clearly, if someone hurt you, there’s something wrong with you to deserve it. For Stella, it was her autism.<br /><br />If it were obvious and unmistakable at any point in the book that the author was highlighting this attitude as a <strong>problem</strong>, I might feel more kindly disposed toward it. Instead, it’s relying on the misguided belief that autism is an inherent flaw that you’re supposed to overcome, and it’s positioning the love interest, Michael, as someone who will, and I quote, “seduce [perhaps more aptly termed in this context: <em>fuck</em>] the anxiety out of [Stella]”, <strong>failing to examine the crucial fact that Stella’s past sexual encounters didn’t go awry because of her autism—her past dates were simply pieces of shit who didn’t treat her like a human being. </strong>And then, Michael comes along, shows Stella the barest scrapings of human decency, and she feeds off that, because she’s been starving and thought such crumbs a feast.<br /><br />It’s like the novel version of those heterosexual dating articles whose entire premise is basically: “How To Hack Men Into Treating You Like a Person.”<br /><br />This is a frustration exacerbated by the fact that once Stella establishes that she enjoys physical contact with a man (read: a man who treats her decently and who doesn’t leave her laying on the bed like an unloved doll splayed out on the floor), she suggests that they now forgo the sex altogether and work together to figure out how to make her comfortable in romantic situations, and so begins a fake-relationship which of course blossoms into a romance.<br /><br />I fault this book for trying to depict a well-balanced pairing only to deploy it in ways that feel manipulative and disingenuous. <strong>The bar was already set so low for Michael…and yet, he still managed to slide right under it. </strong>Michael says all the right things to make Stella feel comfortable, but his words stand in blatant contrast against his actions—which were infuriatingly manipulative and alarming. For instance, when Stella clearly voices her discomfort with something, Michael sweeps aside her comments like you’d brush crumbs from a table and assures her that she’ll enjoy it when she tries it, and of course, she does<strong>—</strong>her agency completely disregarded by this point. The relentless patronizing Michael was subtly practicing throughout this book left a deeper impression than anything else, and I couldn't just chalk it up to character unreliability. <br /><br />Also egregious is how Stella’s symptoms seem to conveniently disappear around Michael. In fact, it was pretty obvious early on that the narrative was charitably embellishing Michael’s traits, palliating his possessiveness, and only illuminating his character by <em>villainizing</em> literally every single other male character. This is made even more manifest in the second love interest, Philip, Stella’s coworker, who is painstakingly one-dimensional: he’s an unmitigated jerk. That’s it. That’s the extent of his contribution. I can’t overstate how exhausted I am of this trope. If the romance in your book is only inevitable because every character who’s not the potential love interest is an unbearable asshole…maybe you have a problem.<br /><br />Speaking of problems, there was a particular scene in the beginning that stirred the most unpleasant riots of emotions in me: Philip comes into Stella’s office, casually asks her if she’s a virgin and gives an unsolicited advice from “a man who’s been around the block a few times” (I rolled my eyes so far back I could see the last of my brain cells dying) which is that if she went out and fucked a lot more men, she’d be more experienced and have more luck. The entire scene was howling “sexual harassment in a workplace” and, in the wake of the #MeToo movement, the fact that this whole encounter was carelessly glossed over was extremely disappointing.<br /><br />I'm still very frustrated by this book's refusal to explore and thoroughly examine so many prominent ideas in favor of escalating a plot that keeps a very tight, narrow focus on a romance with really questionable dynamics. I do recognize, however, the importance of books like <em>The Kiss Quotient </em>and how they help improve awareness and diagnosis rates for this under-represented group and I hope to see a greater plurality of representation for autism.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4140342267078987955" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2372264192" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2372264192" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2372264192?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780451490803" href="/book/show/36577586-the-kiss-quotient">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2372264192" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13477171577020971991">4 1/2 stars. Well, <i>this book</i>. I'm not even sure where to start. I guess I'll begin with an overview.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36199084.The_Kiss_Quotient__The_Kiss_Quotient___1_' title='The Kiss Quotient (The Kiss Quotient, #1) by Helen Hoang' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Kiss Quotient</a> is a seriously sexy, fun book that has rekindled my interest in the romance genre. When it hits the spot, I LOVE a good romance, but I rarely find one that goes beyond cliches and instalove so I usually end up bored. Not with this one. Not one bit.<br/><br/>It's the <b>perfect blend of sweet and steamy</b>. And let me be clear: this is not YA. There's a lot of graphic sex scenes, though I should </span>
  <span id="freeText13477171577020971991" style="display:none">4 1/2 stars. Well, <i>this book</i>. I'm not even sure where to start. I guess I'll begin with an overview.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36199084.The_Kiss_Quotient__The_Kiss_Quotient___1_" title="The Kiss Quotient (The Kiss Quotient, #1) by Helen Hoang" rel="nofollow noopener">The Kiss Quotient</a> is a seriously sexy, fun book that has rekindled my interest in the romance genre. When it hits the spot, I LOVE a good romance, but I rarely find one that goes beyond cliches and instalove so I usually end up bored. Not with this one. Not one bit.<br /><br />It's the <b>perfect blend of sweet and steamy</b>. And let me be clear: this is not YA. There's a lot of graphic sex scenes, though I should also say that the author builds up to it really well; she knows how to tease us. It was just so nice to read a book where sex is actually sexy and not political, cold, a form of manipulation, or not sex at all because consent went out the window.<br /><br />This is an ownvoices book about Stella, who has Asperger's syndrome. Convinced she needs lessons on how to be good at sex and relationships, she hires Michael, an escort, to teach her. Michael is mixed race - Vietnamese and Swedish - and described as a hotter version of k-drama star Daniel Henney. In a gender-reversed <i>Pretty Woman</i> scenario, the two inevitably end up developing feelings for one another.<br /><br />Stella's autism makes it difficult for her to know how to behave around other people, and she also struggles with being touched. Through this, the author explores the <b>importance of consent</b> - Michael is deeply respectful of her boundaries and always waits for her to be 100% ready. Perhaps it sounds less sexy than the spontaneous grab-and-go on the office desk sex but it actually isn't. It's kinda wonderful.<br /><br />Okay, and here's the weird thing. I don't know how to talk about this or if I really should, but I think it is worth mentioning. We talk about the importance of diverse books all the time and the way voices by POC, LGBT+, and those with disabilities are absolutely essential. They foster understanding and help a lot of people realize they are not alone. Well, I got a lesson in just how important books like this can be.<br /><br />As I was reading about Stella, I started to make some comparisons. I was so affected by it that I made a list. This list:<br /><br />• Extreme social anxiety<br />• Loss of focus; frequent "zoning out"<br />• Fanatic obsession with a small number of interests<br />• Difficulty reading verbal cues and understanding sarcasm<br />• No interest in playing with others as a young child<br />• Avoiding eye contact or overcompensating and staring<br />• Clumsiness and poor spacial awareness<br />• Called "quiet" "shy" "weird" and "odd"<br />• Outbursts of anger when losing or unable to complete a task<br />• Deep levels of frustration and anxiety when routine disturbed<br />• Practicing "conversation trees" in head<br />• Facial tics <br /><br />Um, yeah. So this is me. Some of these are behaviours I exhibited as a child, but many I still do. It turns out I probably have high functioning autism, formerly known as Asperger's Syndrome. I currently only have a self-diagnosis and a score of 35 out of 40 on the Cambridge autism test (over 32 is high probability of autism) but I am pursuing a professional diagnosis.<br /><br />Huh.<br /><br />Honestly, this book just made me feel so... understood. Everything that I've worked so hard to hide and bury about myself is normalized and even celebrated. So yeah, it is sexy as hell and really sweet, but it's also so important. Seeing as <a href="https://musingsofanaspie.com/2012/08/30/aspergers-differences-in-girls-and-boys/" rel="nofollow noopener">so many women and girls go undiagnosed</a>, this book could offer validation to so many who need it.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13477171577020971991" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2404650553" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2404650553" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2404650553?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Cristina Monica by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/43622386-rachel-aranda">Rachel Aranda</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=autism">autism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=diversity-yay">diversity-yay</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=adult">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2404650553" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7741290332430111245">I am… not impressed.<br/><br/>How lovely that this is an #ownvoices novel. Stella is autistic, as is the author, and so, no one can say that it is not authentic.<br/><br/>But the storyline is not, however, very realistic.<br/><br/>See, Stella is bad at sex, or so she says. She’s also bad at relationships and human interactions in general. So she hires Michael, an escort, to teach her a thing or two.<br/><br/>Or three. *suggestive eyebrows*<br/><br/>I was entertained for the first fifty or so pages, then I became tired of the sex talk. Do we rea</span>
  <span id="freeText7741290332430111245" style="display:none">I am… not impressed.<br /><br />How lovely that this is an #ownvoices novel. Stella is autistic, as is the author, and so, no one can say that it is not authentic.<br /><br />But the storyline is not, however, very realistic.<br /><br />See, Stella is bad at sex, or so she says. She’s also bad at relationships and human interactions in general. So she hires Michael, an escort, to teach her a thing or two.<br /><br />Or three. *suggestive eyebrows*<br /><br />I was entertained for the first fifty or so pages, then I became tired of the sex talk. Do we really need to talk about it in every single page? No, we don’t. <br /><br />I was expecting a smart romance, but it really isn’t that original. Of course, the fact that the main character is autistic is a breath of fresh air, but I didn’t connect with her. I *understood* her – she’s pretty straightforward and eloquent – but none of the characters felt particularly three dimensional to me.<br /><br />It’s a lot of will they/won’t they, but the reader knows that they will. Come on. So the fact that the protagonists are so confused about their feelings for one another gets old fast and becomes rather annoying. Enough! <br /><br />It also isn’t… romantic. Or extremely sexy. It’s steamy at times – what with all the sex/foreplay I sure hope so – but it didn’t summon stars in my eyes (or, something else…) and I will soon forget about this couple. It didn’t help that the writing was quite dry. <br /><br />I know. This is an important book. But I won’t rate a book highly if it didn’t win my heart, especially considering that there are other *important* novels out there that actually managed to claim a place on my list of favourites. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7741290332430111245" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2407297782" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2407297782" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2407297782?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Melanie by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/16219087-chelsea-chelseadolling-reads">Chelsea (chelseadolling reads)</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=erotic-scenes">erotic-scenes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=own-voices">own-voices</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2407297782" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4453178829853766409"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529528354i/25826975._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>This was my pick for the June 2018 <a href='https://www.mybotm.com/0qjpd8iptc5p' rel='nofollow noopener'>Book of the Month</a> box!<br/><br/><i>ARC provided by the publisher via Netgalley in exchange for an honest review.</i><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I like you better than calculus, and math is the only thing that unites the universe.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Friends, <i>The Kiss Quotient</i> is so deserving of every ounce of hype it has received thus far. I am not sure I’ve ever been so happy, and had such a lame grin on my face, while reading any other book. This was heartwarming, beautiful, and a treat to read. Don’t sleep on</span>
  <span id="freeText4453178829853766409" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529528354i/25826975._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This was my pick for the June 2018 <a href="https://www.mybotm.com/0qjpd8iptc5p" rel="nofollow noopener">Book of the Month</a> box!<br><br><i>ARC provided by the publisher via Netgalley in exchange for an honest review.</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I like you better than calculus, and math is the only thing that unites the universe.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Friends, <i>The Kiss Quotient</i> is so deserving of every ounce of hype it has received thus far. I am not sure I’ve ever been so happy, and had such a lame grin on my face, while reading any other book. This was heartwarming, beautiful, and a treat to read. Don’t sleep on this one. Also, Michael and Stella are both partner goals, I swear. <br><br>This is an ownvoices novel about a high-functioning autistic woman who has succeeded in every aspect of her life, except for love. Her mother is putting pressure on her to find someone and start thinking about family, now that she turned thirty. Plus, Stella is kind of lonely anyway, and as much as she loves throwing herself into her work, she wants to spend her life with someone who she can completely be herself with. The problem is, Stella thinks her autism makes her unable to successfully date, and maybe even unable to be good at/enjoy sex. So, she hires the dreamiest escort to help her! <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Girls like me intimidate boyfriends away. Girls like me have never been asked out by a single boy. Girls like me have to find their own way, make their own luck. I’ve had to fight for every success in my life, and I’m going to fight for this. I’m going to get good at sex, and then I’ll finally be able to entice the right person into being mine.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>The thing is, Michael is an escort that doesn’t do more than one session per client. Yet, after his and Stella’s first night, he might be willing to make an exception. Michael is biracial (Vietnamese and Swedish), fashion designer, and has always put his family first, especially after the way his father left them all. Michael’s mother is also battling cancer, and the medical bills are piling up. <br><br><b>Trigger and content warnings</b> for unwanted touching and forced kissing, lowkey sexual harassment, anxiety attacks, abandonment, a loved one with a chronic illness, a fatphobic comment/insult, and someone telling someone else about a person’s diagnosis. <br><br>Also, this book has very explicit and graphic sex scenes. But, like, all of the sex scenes in this book are 11/10. So damn hot, I swear. I have a lot more experience with sex than Stella, but I would happily let Michael teach me a thing or two. *clutches pearls forever* But please use caution if that is something you do not enjoy in your books!<br><br>But besides the steamy sex, the beautiful romance, and the lovely messages that are inside this book, my favorite part is that this book never shames Michael for being an escort, and it sure in the hell doesn’t shame Stella for being on the autism spectrum. A lot of other conflicts happen throughout, but those two things are never put in a negative light and it was such a blessing. <br><br>And I never expect a fiction book to teach me anything, but this book gave me such a wonderful glimpse and perspective into some people’s autism. (Obviously, I know that no two people are the same!) From overstimulation with lights, sounds, and smells, to the preferred clothing, to focusing everything into one thing, to the importance of schedules, lists, and reminders! This book was really insightful, and I loved that about it. <br><br>The importance of consent is always at the forefront of this novel. I think that’s why most people who are reading this right now are so in love with Michael, and it’s because he always is thoughtful and so very patient with Stella. He truly puts her needs first, and makes sure he is never overstepping any line that she is not willing to cross. <br><br>And I just loved Stella Lane as a character. She is actually probably my favorite heroine of 2018. Not only does she know who she is, she refuses to change for anyone, even the guy she has fallen in love with. I had happy tears in my eyes so much while reading this, and it was mostly just because I was so proud of her. Michael might be most people’s wet dream, but Stella felt like the character I’ve been searching literature for forever. <br> <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“But I want you to know I can handle the truth. If I’m not enough for you, that’s fair and I accept it. I’ll get over you eventually. I don’t want to be coddled or lied to because of what I am. I don’t need your pity friendship”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Overall, this was such a perfect read! I loved this from first to last page, and I couldn’t put it down. Here, I’ll really sell you on how good this book is: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1958236129" rel="nofollow noopener">Muse of Nightmares</a>, my most anticipated release of 2018, came in the mail while I was reading this book. And you know what I did? I finished <i>The Kiss Quotient</i> before starting it. Seriously, this is a masterpiece. And I can’t wait to see what Helen Hoang does next. <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a> <br><br><i>The quotes above were taken from an ARC and are subject to change upon publication.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4453178829853766409" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3328058666" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3328058666" />
    <a title="Cindy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57797254-cindy"><img alt="Cindy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598112512p2/57797254.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3328058666?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy" href="/user/show/57797254-cindy">Cindy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3328058666" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5332594993699675948">3.5 or 4? Not sure, but I’ll bump it up on Goodreads just because I personally enjoyed it despite some of its faults! It’s a cute, light, and fluffy read with very minimal conflict and stakes, making this an easy and simple book to indulge myself in a mental break. The relationship dynamics (the successful woman + the sweet guy who pines after her and thinks she’s too good for him) and the male love interest (so patient and sensitive!) are right up my alley, and I also enjoyed the smut scenes fo</span>
  <span id="freeText5332594993699675948" style="display:none">3.5 or 4? Not sure, but I’ll bump it up on Goodreads just because I personally enjoyed it despite some of its faults! It’s a cute, light, and fluffy read with very minimal conflict and stakes, making this an easy and simple book to indulge myself in a mental break. The relationship dynamics (the successful woman + the sweet guy who pines after her and thinks she’s too good for him) and the male love interest (so patient and sensitive!) are right up my alley, and I also enjoyed the smut scenes for how steamy they were.<br /><br />Downsides: it’s very instalove-y to the point where it can be distractingly unrealistic and contrived, though I tried my best to just go with it haha. And though I didn’t mind minimal conflict for the sake of light reading, when the book does try to ramp up with conflict towards the end, it’s done with very contrived miscommunication that was a little frustrating and too drawn out. The sudden character development in gaining confidence also felt thrown in for the sake of wrapping up the story. I think the book is better when it goes along with the light and fluffy moments and smutty scenes, rather than trying to add conflict or narrative developments, which doesn’t work as well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5332594993699675948" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2427907371" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2427907371" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9684061-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528750408p2/9684061.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2427907371?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/9684061-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=predictable">predictable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2427907371" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10219558470140339049"><i>Not exactly the wow-worthy read I was expecting.</i><br/><br/>There’s been a ton of buzz surrounding this novel and I would say, rightly so for <u>one</u> reason. With this story, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17147855.Helen_Hoang' title='Helen Hoang' rel='nofollow noopener'>Helen Hoang</a> gives voice to a syndrome that until now has been absent in the romance genre. Through her cast of endearing characters, she explores the importance of self-acceptance and the desire we all have to find that one person who makes establishing an intimate relationship feel effortless. <b>I just wish I had enjoyed the plot as much as</b></span>
  <span id="freeText10219558470140339049" style="display:none"><i>Not exactly the wow-worthy read I was expecting.</i><br /><br />There’s been a ton of buzz surrounding this novel and I would say, rightly so for <u>one</u> reason. With this story, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17147855.Helen_Hoang" title="Helen Hoang" rel="nofollow noopener">Helen Hoang</a> gives voice to a syndrome that until now has been absent in the romance genre. Through her cast of endearing characters, she explores the importance of self-acceptance and the desire we all have to find that one person who makes establishing an intimate relationship feel effortless. <b>I just wish I had enjoyed the plot as much as the characters she created.</b> Viewing the world through an autistic lens brings a fresh energy to the storyline <u>initially</u>, but it doesn't take long for the formulaic feel of the plot to overshadow the quirkiness of the cast.<br /><br />A gender-swapped <i>Pretty Woman</i> of sorts, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36199084.The_Kiss_Quotient__The_Kiss_Quotient___1_" title="The Kiss Quotient (The Kiss Quotient, #1) by Helen Hoang" rel="nofollow noopener">The Kiss Quotient</a> introduces the reader to Stella Lane, an incredibly smart and driven, thirty-something, living with high-functioning Asperger’s. Her social awkwardness, lack of interpersonal skills and myriad of other eccentricities have been a hinderance on her relationship status. Her best bet, she figures, is to start by improving her skills in the bedroom. <br /><br />So, how does one go about getting better at sex? I guess, if you’re rich and lacking in social skills, you hire a male escort to teach you a few things. Who better to learn from than a professional, right? Lucky for Stella, Michael is the perfect specimen of a man. Tailor by day, sexual escort every Friday night and all around <i>good</i> guy—what could go wrong? In the real world, probably a lot; but this is fiction. <i>Predictable</i> fiction. <br /><br />What's a romance novel without a happy ending?—it's pretty much a given this is <i>going</i> to happen. Aside from the character traits I admired in both Stella and Michael, their love story felt dare I say . . . <i>basic</i>. Their budding relationship narrowly avoids insta-love, is paved with convenience and the will-they/won't-they is fueled solely by miscommunication on both their parts, which takes on a stale note rather quickly. And while we would all love to fall for someone who completely understand us—no questions asked—it’s unrealistic to think it would ever happen <i>this</i> easily.<br /><br />Despite all of my issues with the plot, I still found this to be a worthwhile read. My big takeaway—<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17147855.Helen_Hoang" title="Helen Hoang" rel="nofollow noopener">Helen Hoang</a>’s message in the <i>Author's Note</i> following Stella and Michael's story—be unapologetically you. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“As I pursued and eventually attained a diagnosis (at age thirty-four), Stella, my autistic heroine, was born on the page. It has never been so easy for me to write a character. I knew her intimately. She came from my heart. I didn’t have to filter my thoughts to make her socially acceptable, something I’d been unconsciously doing for ages. And this freedom allowed me to find my voice. Before this, I’d been using every other author’s writing style, trying to be someone else. When I wrote The Kiss Quotient, I became myself, and I’ve been unapologetically myself ever since. Sometimes instead of confining you, a label can set you free.”</i>
</blockquote><i><br /><br />*Thanks to Berkley for providing my copy.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="10219558470140339049" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2383092760" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2383092760" />
    <a title="Roxane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1151637-roxane"><img alt="Roxane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442511711p2/1151637.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2383092760?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roxane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roxane" href="/user/show/1151637-roxane">Roxane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2383092760" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7407138805611051254">The Kiss Quotient is quite the unexpected romance novel. Stella Lane is on the spectrum and wants to get better at sex so she can, hopefully, find a life partner and start the family her parents so very much want her to have. To get better at sex she hires Michael, an escort with a lot of debt and a few secrets but who, somehow, is exactly the man she needs. Of course he is! That's how romance novels work. But this is such a fun read and it's also quite original and sexy and sensitive. Stella is</span>
  <span id="freeText7407138805611051254" style="display:none">The Kiss Quotient is quite the unexpected romance novel. Stella Lane is on the spectrum and wants to get better at sex so she can, hopefully, find a life partner and start the family her parents so very much want her to have. To get better at sex she hires Michael, an escort with a lot of debt and a few secrets but who, somehow, is exactly the man she needs. Of course he is! That's how romance novels work. But this is such a fun read and it's also quite original and sexy and sensitive. Stella is a really compelling protagonist and Hoang does a fine job of showing us who this woman is and how she negotiates a world that isn't as welcoming to her as she deserves. Lots to admire her! Well worth a read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7407138805611051254" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2277204893" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2277204893" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2277204893?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2018-audio">2018-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2018-five-stars">2018-five-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2277204893" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10989176909203991774"><b>5+ Stars!!!</b> <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525261381i/25469795._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>There isn't much better as a reader than finding a debut novel that you have zero expectations for, and it blowing you away. <i>The Kiss Quotient</i> did just that. Helen Hoang wrote a book that is smart, sexy, made me laugh, and gave me just the right amount of feels. There wasn't one thing I would change about this story or the characters. I loved everything about it! <br/><br/>Stella Lane is a thirty year old econometrician who is smart and successful, but lacking in one area of her life. Relatio</span>
  <span id="freeText10989176909203991774" style="display:none"><b>5+ Stars!!!</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525261381i/25469795._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>There isn't much better as a reader than finding a debut novel that you have zero expectations for, and it blowing you away. <i>The Kiss Quotient</i> did just that. Helen Hoang wrote a book that is smart, sexy, made me laugh, and gave me just the right amount of feels. There wasn't one thing I would change about this story or the characters. I loved everything about it! <br><br>Stella Lane is a thirty year old econometrician who is smart and successful, but lacking in one area of her life. Relationships. After her mother pressuring her to settle down and meet someone, Stella decides it's time she gives it a try. Stella has Aspergers, a high-functioning form of Autism that makes her a little awkward when it comes to relationships, sex, and certain social situations. Due to this, she decides to hire an escort to 'teach' her how to navigate this. <br><br>This is where Michael enters. Michael is an escort, but he's so much more than that. He is a stand-up guy who only escorts on Friday nights as a way to help his family financially. Honestly, he feels that he has no choice. When he meets Stella, he is stunned someone like her would hire an escort. She fascinates him. Michael is kind to Stella, he's patient and understanding to her situation. So much so, that being with him one night won't do. <br><i>
  <blockquote>These were supposed to be simple sex lessons. Why was it getting so complicated?</blockquote>
</i><br>Michael and Stella develop a friendship and relationship of sorts. One of my favorite things about this book was seeing how Michael grew to care for Stella, embraced her quirks and handled everything that made her different. Both of these characters made my heart so happy. I adored them both and wanted nothing more than their relationship/friendship to go to the next level. <br><br>One thing I found so refreshing about this book is Stella's character. I could tell Hoang knew what she was talking about when she wrote Stella. Even though Stella is much different than me, she was very relateable.  Michael and Stella brought out the best in one another and their connection and chemistry were off the charts. <br><br><i>The Kiss Quotient</i> is quite honestly one of the best books I've read this year. It was perfection. The story is refreshing and unique, and the writing is intelligent and fresh. I can't wait to see what else Helen Hoang has in store. I'll definitely be reading every and anything else she puts out! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525261381i/25469796._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="10989176909203991774" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16623584956803133320"><b>
  <i>“I’m obsessed with you, Michael,” she confessed.</i>
</b><br/><br/>I want to hug this book. But since I don't have the physical copy of it yet, I'm going to have to be satisfied with hugging my kindle. <br/>The story was even better the second time round. I remember the miscommunication bugging me when it happened the first time I read it. Now, I'm realising us humans do have a major issue with communicating because we're uncomfortable with being vulnerable. <br/><br/>I appreciated even more how unapologetic Stella became. H</span>
  <span id="freeText16623584956803133320" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“I’m obsessed with you, Michael,” she confessed.</i>
</b><br /><br />I want to hug this book. But since I don't have the physical copy of it yet, I'm going to have to be satisfied with hugging my kindle. <br />The story was even better the second time round. I remember the miscommunication bugging me when it happened the first time I read it. Now, I'm realising us humans do have a major issue with communicating because we're uncomfortable with being vulnerable. <br /><br />I appreciated even more how unapologetic Stella became. How comfortable she became in her skin. It was so powerful to read. <br />This story was just so pure and wholesome. My heart is full. <br /><br />---------------------------<br /><br />I confess that I am obsessed with this book. These characters. I had problems breathing properly on several occasions. Why did no one prepare me for the amount of damn, steamy scenes were going to be in this book?!<br /><br />I could’ve died just by swooning, good lord.<br /><br />Stella is my hero. Michael is my husband. (Book-boyfriend is too short term!) I need this man in my life. <br /><br />I’m liking that more and more romance novels are coming out now that have substance and depth to them. In the past, they were pure enjoyment for me and they still are, but I was learning so much about high-functioning autism whilst reading this book.<br />I also liked the insight we got of someone who became an escort and getting a slight glimpse into that world.<br /><br />It just reinforces how much I love fiction. Storytelling is the most perfect of ways to understand others, because there are emotions that get triggered when we read that allows us to form a bond to the story and its characters. <br />It leads us to remember specific aspects of the story that have touched us the most, because it deals with subject matters that make us fundamentally human. <br /><br />And they say fiction isn’t educational.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16623584956803133320" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2298202156" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2298202156" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2298202156?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780451490803" href="/book/show/36577586-the-kiss-quotient">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=the-best-of-the-best">the-best-of-the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=disability-and-mi">disability-and-mi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=steamy">steamy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2298202156" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9663302381406781154"><blockquote>#1 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2298202156' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Kiss Quotient</a> ★★★★★<br/>#2 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2584292034' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Bride Test</a> ★★★★☆</blockquote><br/>Sometimes, you hear so much hype for a book that you reach the point where you’re almost afraid to read it, because your hopes are so high that you just know, if it disappoints you even an iota, you’re going to be totally crushed… right? It’s the worst feeling and it can make it so hard to finally pick up that superlatively popular read, because nobody wants to be the only person who hates a book, right?<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “All the things that make you diffe</i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText9663302381406781154" style="display:none"><blockquote>#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2298202156" rel="nofollow noopener">The Kiss Quotient</a> ★★★★★<br />#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2584292034" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bride Test</a> ★★★★☆</blockquote><br />Sometimes, you hear so much hype for a book that you reach the point where you’re almost afraid to read it, because your hopes are so high that you just know, if it disappoints you even an iota, you’re going to be totally crushed… right? It’s the worst feeling and it can make it so hard to finally pick up that superlatively popular read, because nobody wants to be the only person who hates a book, right?<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “All the things that make you different make you perfect.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Nah, I’m just playing with you guys—this book was <b>everything I ever hoped it would be and more.</b> Oh, my gosh, I cannot even describe how much I adored this book! I literally picked it up with the goal of reading a few chapters for my buddy read, and <b>
  <i>bam!</i>
</b>, it was way past my bedtime and I was sitting here in some sort of shocked state, like, “How do I even follow up how freaking <i>perfect</i> that was?!”<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>She wasn’t broken. She saw and interacted with the world in a different way, but that was her.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Seriously, <i>The Kiss Quotient</i> is worth every single ounce of hype it has received and so much more. The chemistry is on fire, the story is so fun and captivating, and these characters—you can’t help but love them. Stella is incredible. I loved being inside her head, and knowing that it’s own-voice autism rep, I wasn’t surprised by how much of what she said mirrored things my own autistic loved ones have shared with me (as well as feelings I myself have had, having strongly suspected that I am autistic for a very long time but never having sought out a diagnosis).<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Michael was mint chocolate chip for her. She could try other flavors, but he’d always be her favorite.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />While Stella is the star, Michael is honestly just as lovable and precious as she is. He’s this biracial Vietnamese/Swedish man, though the only family we meet of his is the Vietnamese side, and they are all so lovable and wonderful, even down to his obnoxious sisters. I loved every scene in his mother’s home, I loved his dedication to his mother and family in general, and I just cherished all of Michael’s motives and inner dialogue so much.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “I don’t want just a night or a week or a month with you. I want you all the time.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Between the cuteness, the math, the fake dating trope done <i>flawlessly</i>, the steamy sweet moments, and the fantastic focus on consent… I honestly have nothing but good things to say about <i>The Kiss Quotient</i>. Instead of rambling on, I’ll just echo the tons of other people saying <b>if you haven’t read this book, you need to!</b> It’s wonderful, charming, sad, heavy, and sweet, all wrapped up into one emotional little bundle of romance, sex, and family.<br /><br />———<br /><br />Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2552065986" rel="nofollow noopener">Owl</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9663302381406781154" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2150371003" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2150371003" />
    <a title="Penelope Douglas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21474351-penelope-douglas"><img alt="Penelope Douglas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480874866p2/21474351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2150371003?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Penelope Douglas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Penelope Douglas" href="/user/show/21474351-penelope-douglas">Penelope Douglas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2150371003" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10064227851316935606">I started reading this Friday night on a plane, and as usual, I suspected I probably wouldn't make it past chapter 3 before just putting on my headphones and opening up my laptop to write instead. Most of my readers know I don't read much romance anymore, not because it's not good, but because I write it all day, I kind of need a break when I'm reading for pleasure. So I veer toward other genres. <br/><br/>It's like a hairstylist, you know? You think their families would constantly be able to get their ha</span>
  <span id="freeText10064227851316935606" style="display:none">I started reading this Friday night on a plane, and as usual, I suspected I probably wouldn't make it past chapter 3 before just putting on my headphones and opening up my laptop to write instead. Most of my readers know I don't read much romance anymore, not because it's not good, but because I write it all day, I kind of need a break when I'm reading for pleasure. So I veer toward other genres. <br /><br />It's like a hairstylist, you know? You think their families would constantly be able to get their hair done, but oh, no. They're the last people to get their hair done! A stylist comes home, that's the last thing they want to do! lol<br /><br />So anyway, I started reading. And I kept reading. By chapter 2 I was laughing. By chapter 3 I was like "oh, yeah." By chapter 5 I was denying my complimentary pretzels and Sprite. And by chapter 12 my tired eyes were glancing between my Kindle screen and the hotel room clock, knowing I had to be up for a signing in 7 hours, and should I go to sleep or...ok, just after this part and then I'll definitely go to bed. <br /><br />The author gives us an incredible hero in this story. He has a tough hurdle to overcome, but he's noble and strong but also incredibly hot. He has just the right amount of edge and a touch of bad boy, but at the same time he's doing what he has to do and he's the only man who understands Stella. This guy from a completely different world than her is the only man who can talk to her and connect with her. When they strip everything away and are alone, close and quiet, they are everything the other one will ever need. <br /><br />Stella is strong and smart, educated and awkward in social situations, and I absolutely loved her. I connected with her. What built between these pages was a relationship between a striving woman and the man she hired to help her, both of whom never expected or tried to make it happen. It wasn't supposed to happen. The lines of the professional relationship start to blur, and slowly, their bond seals, even as they try to resist it. <br /><br />I loved this story. I loved both of the characters. I adored the side characters and how everything felt natural, the writing flowed, and the heat and need and longing for someone you're not supposed to fall for got stronger and stronger. <br /><br />And I really wish Hoang had more books out right now!<br /><br />Give this one a try when it releases, everyone! You won't be sorry!! And I can't wait to read your thoughts. And have others to swoon with &lt;3 Because I feel so alone right now. Lol</span>
  <a data-text-id="10064227851316935606" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2367712853" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2367712853" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2367712853?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780451490803" href="/book/show/36577586-the-kiss-quotient">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those who want to like romances, but never find good ones</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Tatiana by: </span>
      PW
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=romancelandia">romancelandia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2367712853" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7103478302735149479">Alright, I am just going to up my rating to 5 stars. I devoured every sweet, smutty page of this story. Again. While I am not blind to this romance’s flaws, I simply love it. I feel like this story was written exclusively for me. <br/><br/><b>Original review </b><br/>The last time I enjoyed a romance novel this much was... hm, I think the word I am reaching for is NEVER. I am always looking for good love stories but rarely find them. This book scratched my romance itch <b>just right</b>. I pretty much loved it.<br/><br/>So the setup </span>
  <span id="freeText7103478302735149479" style="display:none">Alright, I am just going to up my rating to 5 stars. I devoured every sweet, smutty page of this story. Again. While I am not blind to this romance’s flaws, I simply love it. I feel like this story was written exclusively for me. <br /><br /><b>Original review </b><br />The last time I enjoyed a romance novel this much was... hm, I think the word I am reaching for is NEVER. I am always looking for good love stories but rarely find them. This book scratched my romance itch <b>just right</b>. I pretty much loved it.<br /><br />So the setup goes like this. An autistic econometritian unable to form relationships and under pressure from her mom to start a family hires a male escort to teach how to “be good at sex” so she knows how to attract and keep a man. She doesn’t really like to be touched, so this challenge is no joke. If you’ve read romances or at least watched Pretty Woman, you can see what happens next. The escort Stella hires is hot and fun, and most importantly, kind.<br /><br />You know how you read something soul-crushing like <a href="https://www.newyorker.com/magazine/2017/12/11/cat-person" rel="nofollow noopener">Cat Person </a> or <a href="https://babe.net/2018/01/13/aziz-ansari-28355" rel="nofollow noopener">that notorious recap of a date with Aziz Ansari </a> and get nauseous and depressed? Well “The Kissing Quotient” is the opposite of that. It is a celebration of human connection, consent, pleasure and, as clinical as it sounds, enthusiastically reading the other person’s nonverbal cues.<br /><br />As it always happens with romance novels, I did lose a little interest once the hottest part was over and the inevitable dramatic breakup started unfolding before the final sprint to HEA (I am not really keen on wedding, engagements, babies, etc.) To the author’s credit, the novel mostly stayed away from tedious misunderstandings I loathe.<br /><br />But all in all this was a fantastic experience. A romance equally hot and sweet.<br /><br />You can request it on Netgalley.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7103478302735149479" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2458846971?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=autism">autism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2458846971" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13940300447058588138"><b>Aww how cute is this?!</b> I wanted to read this because of the #ownvoices autistic storyline, but hesitated for <i>ages</i> because...adult romance is not my thing lmao. But I was too curious not to try, so here I am and my opinion is seriously: AWW HOW CUTE IS THIS.<br/><br/>It almost reminded me of Lara Jean x Peter Kavinsky...with the fake dating. But grown up. And with a lot of sex. And he's an escort and she's an autistic and works in economics instead. ¯\_(ツ)_/¯ So um nothing alike but the FAKE DATING. It's a</span>
  <span id="freeText13940300447058588138" style="display:none"><b>Aww how cute is this?!</b> I wanted to read this because of the #ownvoices autistic storyline, but hesitated for <i>ages</i> because...adult romance is not my thing lmao. But I was too curious not to try, so here I am and my opinion is seriously: AWW HOW CUTE IS THIS.<br /><br />It almost reminded me of Lara Jean x Peter Kavinsky...with the fake dating. But grown up. And with a lot of sex. And he's an escort and she's an autistic and works in economics instead. ¯\_(ツ)_/¯ So um nothing alike but the FAKE DATING. It's a freaking good trope.<br /><br /><b>It was really addictive to read.</b> I powered through it in a few hours and it was sweet and soft and kind. Like woah give us a man like Michael who: sews, has lots of sisters that he takes care of, he loves and supports his mum like nothing else, he designs clothes, he respects women, he cooks, he's a martial arts dude. afdksal his Michael though. He's also biracial Vietnamese and there's so much family love and culture woven into the story!<br /><br />And their romance was such a slow burn emotional build up. I don't even LIKE solely-romance books but I was just flipping pages, teeth gritted, whispering, "They better frikkin work out or else I love them too much."<br /><br /><b>And the autism rep nearly made me cry with how perfect it was.</b> I think it's the little things that made it so real, so accurate, and so so up-lifting. And also at the end when Stella says a big loud NO to changing herself and just says: <i>I am autistic and this is who I am and I'm not broken.</i> And I'm just scREAM cheering in the background. As an autistic myself, late diagnosed too, I just totally fell in love with Stella. She's not a stereotype! She's kind and loving and sweet, and also super sensitive and fixated on routines and obsessions.<b> If you want to read a book to really see what it's like being an autistic woman = CHOOSE THIS ONE.</b><br /><br /><b>This book has given me all mushy feels. Aww</b>. It was two people genuinely falling in love while convinced the other didn't love them that was so good to read. And good autism rep!? And sweet characters who I both loved incredibly. THIS WAS SOFT™. (But like...a lot of sex lmao. I mainly read YA so this was a bit 0_0 for me, but still.)</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
